    [Original] Insufflation Unit Recall: Olympus Removes High Flow Insufflation Units
    The affected products and recommendations for what to do with the devices below have not changed. This recall involves removing certain devices from where they are used or sold. The FDA has identified this recall as the most serious type. This device may cause serious injury or death if you continue to use it. The FDA is aware that Olympus has issued a letter to affected customers recommending certain High Flow Insufflation Units be removed from where they are used or sold. Affected devices: Do not use affected devices. Identify and quarantine affected devices immediately. On January 16, 2026, Olympus sent all affected customers a letter recommending the following actions: Olympus stated that the software algorithm on High Flow Insufflation Unit, models UHI, UHI-2, and UHI-3, requires correction to address a potential issue which could lead to overpressure events. These products have been discontinued and have not been supported by repair for many years. Because no corrective solution is available for the affected models, Olympus has decided to remove these devices from the market. Over insufflation may lead to various patient harms during a procedure, including air embolism, arrythmias (bradycardia, asystole, or cardiac arrest), pneumothorax, kidney or urinary problems, hypoxia, subcutaneous emphysema, delay to treatment, more complex procedures, and potentially death. As of December 31, Olympus has reported two serious injuries, and no deaths associated with this issue. The UHI, UHI-2, and UHI-3 High Flow Insufflation Unit models are designed to insufflate the abdominal cavity and provide automatic suction and smoke evacuation to facilitate laparoscopic observation and treatment. Customers in the U.S. with adverse reactions, quality problems, or questions about this recall should contact Olympus at 1- 800-848-9024 and select option 1. Health care professionals and consumers may report adverse reactions or quality problems they experienced using these devices to MedWatch: The FDA Safety Information and Adverse Event Reporting Program.

    [Original] CDMO Bora locks in 5-year, $250M production agreement with GSK
    Feb 23, 2026 12:02pm Bora Pharmaceuticals CDMO contract manufacturing Facilities --> With a productive working relationship between the two companies already well established, Bora Pharmaceuticals is renewing a $250 million global manufacturing agreement with British drugmaker GSK. The deal, which covers a five-year term, will see the CDMO chip in on hundreds of products across an array of therapeutic areas. The production tie-up covers end-to-end manufacturing services for more than 20 commercial GSK product lines and over 335 individual products in indications spanning HIV, malaria, pneumonia, parasitic infections, depression, migraine, acne, eczema and psoriasis, Bora said in a Feb. 23 press release. Much of the contract manufacturing work will revolve around Boraâ€™s Mississauga, Ontario, facility in Canada, and the collaboration will also grant GSK access to additional sites within Bora's network, including a new oral solid-dose plant in Minnesota. The partnership builds on a longstanding relationship between GSK and Bora, with Bora picking up its Mississauga facility from the British Big Pharma in 2020. As it stands, GSK is the largest pharma partner operating at Boraâ€™s Ontario site, according to the CDMO. With the deal, GSK will â€œcontinue to leverage Boraâ€™s experienced development teams and global commercial manufacturing infrastructureâ€ to maintain an uninterrupted supply of key GSK medicines, Bora noted in its release. â€œFrom day one, this partnership was built on mutual trust and a shared commitment to quality,â€ Bora CEO Bobby Sheng explained in a statement. â€œReaching nearly a decade of collaboration with GSK and committing through 2030 speaks to our shared focus on value and reliability," he continued. "Weâ€™re grateful for the opportunity to continue supporting GSKâ€™s mission and the patients who rely on these therapies.â€ Bora has been busy building out its Mississauga site since it acquired the plant in late 2020. Investments in flexible manufacturing technology have enabled the site to support 32 clients, advance 61 products and complete more than 400 project and development batches, according to Bora, which described the plant as a "strategic manufacturing partner for leading global pharmaceutical companies." The CDMOâ€™s site in Canada occupies 170,000 square feet and offers manufacturing, processing and commercialization services for a range of prescription and over-the-counter products, including oral solid-dose, liquid and semi-solid therapeutics, according to Boraâ€™s website. The spot is equipped with 18 â€œhighly configurableâ€ manufacturing modules and packaging capabilities for tablets, capsules, nasal sprays, creams and more. Elsewhere across Boraâ€™s North American footprint, the company operates facilities in Baltimore, Maryland, and Maple Grove, Minnesota. The CDMOâ€™s four other manufacturing spots are spread across Taiwan. Bora has been on a speedy growth track in North America in recent years. Last summer, the company announced an upgrade to the manufacturing and packaging capacity at its Maple Grove site, which it picked up through its $210 million Upsher-Smith buyout in 2024. Meanwhile, Bora recently acquired its first sterile manufacturing facility in Baltimore through a 2024 agreement with Emergent BioSolutions.

    [Original] Fortress sells FDA voucher for $205M after Zycubo approval last month
    Feb 23, 2026 10:15am priority review voucher FDA Fortress Biotech Rare Pediatric Disease Priority Review Voucher --> Only a month after Jazz Pharmaceuticals said it had signed a deal to sell an FDA priority review voucher (PRV) for $200 million, a new PRV transaction involving Fortress Biotech and an unnamed buyer shows that the trend of rising voucher prices is still going strong. Monday morning, Fortress said its subsidiary, Cyprium Therapeutics, has entered into an agreement to sell a recently received rare pediatric disease priority review voucher for $205 million. Cyprium got its hands on the PRV as part of the FDA's recent approval of injected copper replacement therapy Zycubo as the first treatment approved in the U.S. for the rare neurodegenerative disorder Menkes disease. While another company, Sentynl Therapeutics, is handling development and commercialization of Zycubo under a 2023 agreement, the deal called for Sentynl to transfer the PRV back to Fortress/Cyprium after the approval. Following the Jan. 12 approval of Zycubo, Cyprium wasted no time in striking a PRV sale. The $205 million transaction follows last month's disclosure from Jazz that it had agreed to sell its own PRV for $200 million. Before that, PRV transfers last year ranged between $150 million and $175 million. PRVs are awarded in conjunction with certain rare pediatric disease approvals and enable users to shorten FDA reviews from the agency's standard 10-month window to about six months. For a company with a promising launch waiting in the wings, a PRV could be worth hundreds of millions of dollars in order to help speed a highly anticipated drug to market. In the case of Cyprium and Zycubo, the company said it remains eligible for tiered royalties based on the drug's sales and up to $129 million in milestones. Further, the company stressed that it must pay 20% of the PRV sale proceeds to the Eunice Kennedy Shriver National Institute of Child Health and Human Development. The trend of increasing PRV sale values comes even as the FDA advances a new initiative called the commissioner's national priority voucher. Winners of these vouchersâ€”which are handed out at the agency's discretion based on certain national prioritiesâ€”are entitled to ultrafast FDA reviews spanning one to two months. The controversial program has already yielded one rejection, with Disc Medicine's bitopertin being spurned earlier this month.

    [Original] Binance Employees Find $1.7 Billion in Crypto Was Sent to Iranian Entities
    Internal investigators at Binance uncovered that over 1,500 accounts had been accessed by individuals in Iran, with approximately $1.7 billion flowing from Binance accounts to Iranian-linked entities tied to terrorist groups, including the Houthis and Iranâ€™s Revolutionary Guards Corps, a possible violation of U.S. sanctions. One of the accounts involved belonged to a Binance vendor, Blessed Trust, a Hong Kong-based company incorporated in the British Virgin Islands and Cayman Islands. Over two years, $1.2 billion in cryptocurrency moved from Blessed Trustâ€™s Binance account to wallets linked to Iranâ€™s Revolutionary Guards, according to documents reviewed by The New York Times. Blessed Trust served as a fiat partner, facilitating payments and payroll, and listed Binance entities among its top customers. Binance confirmed it severed ties with Blessed Trust in January and reported the findings to U.S. authorities, including the Justice Department and the IRS. A separate investigation revealed that a defunct Hong Kong firm, Hexa Whale Trading Limited, funneled $490 million to Iranian-linked wallets, with Israeli officials alerting Binance to terror financing links. Binance also identified Russian cargo ships using Binance accounts to pay crews, though the vessels were not sanctioned. Despite these findings, Binance suspended or fired at least four internal investigators in November and December 2023, shortly after the Iran-related warnings were raised. The company cited â€œviolations of company protocolâ€ related to unauthorized disclosure of client data, not the reporting of compliance concerns. Rachel Conlan, a Binance spokesperson, stated that the investigation continued and that no employee was disciplined for raising alerts. She emphasized that Binance had fulfilled its legal obligations, noting that detection of logins from sanctioned jurisdictions does not equate to servicing sanctioned persons. The timing of the suspensions, however, raised concerns about retaliation. Over the past months, more than half a dozen compliance officials, including a sanctions manager and the enterprise compliance head, have left the company. Binanceâ€™s chief compliance officer, Noah Perlman, has also considered departing. The revelations come after Binance pleaded guilty in 2023 to violating anti-money-laundering laws and sanctions, agreeing to a $4.3 billion penalty and committing to enhanced compliance. The company has since hired over 60 former law enforcement and regulatory experts. Despite these measures, the internal probe highlights ongoing vulnerabilities. White House press secretary Karoline Leavitt claimed the prior administrationâ€™s prosecution of Binanceâ€™s founder, Changpeng Zhao, was part of a â€œwar on cryptocurrencyâ€ that harmed U.S. innovation. Zhao, who served four months in prison in 2024, was pardoned by President Trump and recently attended a Mar-a-Lago conference, where he posted, â€œLearned a lot.â€ Binance remains the worldâ€™s largest crypto exchange, processing up to two-thirds of global transactions, with Zhao retaining a majority stake and an estimated net worth of $80 billion.

    [Original] Pentagon Summons Anthropic Chief in Dispute Over A.I. Limits
    Amid escalating pressure from the Trump administration, Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth has scheduled a meeting with Dario Amodei, CEO of artificial intelligence firm Anthropic, at the Pentagon to discuss the companyâ€™s use of its technology on classified military systems. The meeting follows a January 9 memo from Hegseth urging AI firms to remove restrictions on their models, prompting renegotiation of a $200 million pilot contract between the Pentagon and Anthropic. While the Defense Department has already signed an agreement with Elon Muskâ€™s xAI and is nearing a deal with Googleâ€”whose Gemini model is seen as a rival to Anthropicâ€”officials aim to use these agreements as leverage to push Anthropic to relax its guardrails. The Pentagon insists contracts must allow unrestricted use of AI models, provided activities remain lawful, while permitting companies to retain safety features, known as â€œthe safety stack.â€ Anthropic, the first company authorized to operate on military classified networks, has agreed to loosen restrictions but demands safeguards against mass surveillance of Americans and deployment of fully autonomous weapons. The company has also taken steps to prevent Chinese entities from accessing its technology, including banning a Chinese-state-sponsored group in November for using its systems in a hacking campaign targeting tech firms, financial institutions, and government agencies. Earlier, OpenAI reported stopping two separate Chinese efforts to use its AI for surveillance. Anthropic recently disclosed that three Chinese AI firms attempted to siphon data from its systems to improve their own models. Pentagon officials acknowledge that removing Anthropic from classified networks would cause short-term disruptions, as military personnel rely on its AI chatbot, Claude, alongside tools from Palantir, for analyzing sensitive data. Experts argue cutting off access would be counterproductive. While Google is eager to secure a dealâ€”having invested heavily in government-exclusive data centers with underutilized capacityâ€”OpenAI remains distant from a classified contract, citing the need to further develop safety protocols. The meeting between Hegseth and Amodei was first reported by Axios. Cade Metz contributed reporting from San Francisco. Julian E. Barnes covers U.S. intelligence and international security; Sheera Frenkel focuses on technologyâ€™s societal impact.

    [Original] ç«‹è®¯ç²¾å¯†ï¼šé¦–æ¬¡å›è´­å…¬å¸è‚¡ä»½990ä¸‡è‚¡ æˆäº¤æ€»é‡‘é¢è¿‘5äº¿å…ƒ
    On February 23, Luxshare Precision (002475.SZ) announced that the company first repurchased 9.9006 million shares through a dedicated securities account for share repurchases via centralized bidding on February 13, 2026, accounting for 0.14% of the company's total share capital. The highest transaction price was 50.91 yuan per share, the lowest was 50.14 yuan per share, and the total transaction amount amounted to 499 million yuan (excluding trading fees). The funds used for this repurchase came from the company's self-raised funds (including special loan funds for share repurchases), and the repurchase price did not exceed 86.60 yuan per share. This repurchase complies with relevant laws, regulations, and the company's previously established share repurchase plan. (Every Economic News Network)

    [Original] åƒé—®ï¼šæ˜¥èŠ‚æœŸé—´ï¼Œç”¨æˆ·åœ¨åƒé—®ä¸Šâ€œä¸€å¥è¯ä¸‹å•â€è¿‘2äº¿æ¬¡
    On the seventh day of the Lunar New Year, February 23, data released by Qwen showed that during the Spring Festival, users placed nearly 200 million one-sentence orders on Qwen. On average, one in every ten people nationwide made an order through Qwen, making requests such as "Qwen, help me buy food and milk tea, book flights and hotels, purchase movie tickets, and reserve tickets for tourist attractions" a new tradition of the Year of the Horse Spring Festival. Stocking up on New Year's goods and drinking milk tea have become the primary consumption scenarios for one-sentence orders. According to statistics, users ordered more than 3,000 tons of eggs through Qwen during the Spring Festival. Meanwhile, users placed a total of 55 million milk tea orders and 35.16 million fruit tea orders, with coffee sales reaching 11.38 million cups.

    [Original] Company director jailed over Â£7m airline parts fraud
    Jose Alejandro Zamora Yrala, 38, has been sentenced to four years and eight months in prison for fraud after running a UK-based company, AOG Technics, that sold Â£7 million worth of aircraft engine parts with falsified documentation. The Serious Fraud Office (SFO) investigation revealed that between 2019 and 2023, Zamora Yrala supplied an estimated 60,000 forged parts for CFM56 enginesâ€”used on Boeing 737s, Airbus A320s, and other aircraftâ€”through a network of fake paperwork. Judge Simon Picken described the actions as a "more or less complete undermining" of aviation safety regulations. Zamora Yrala, who operated from a home office in Surrey, sold parts directly to airlines, maintenance firms, and brokers worldwide. The fraud was uncovered in 2023 when a TAP Air Portugal engineer questioned a partâ€™s origin; the manufacturer confirmed the documentation was fake. This triggered global inspections, grounding aircraft operated by Ryanair, American Airlines, Ethiopian Airlines, and TAP, resulting in Â£39.3 million in estimated losses. Critical Authorised Release Certificates (ARCs), required to verify airworthiness of parts, were falsified. Some were altered versions of genuine certificates obtained from an accomplice technician at an airline, while others were created by a Spanish graphic designer. Zamora Yrala also fabricated supplier records and invented fake employees, including sales and quality managers, to simulate a legitimate business. In reality, only Zamora Yrala, his then-wife, her brother, and the familyâ€™s nanny were on the payroll. The SFO stated it is "almost impossible" to trace the origin of the 60,000 suspect parts now in the global aviation supply chain. Harriet Sassoon, SFO case controller, emphasized the risks posed by unverified components. Alongside his prison sentence, Zamora Yrala has been disqualified from serving as a company director for eight years and will face proceeds of crime proceedings later this year. A related investigation by Portuguese authorities remains ongoing.

    [Original] When is the Spring Statement and what might be in it?
    Chancellor Rachel Reeves will deliver the Spring Statement on 3 March, outlining the latest economic forecasts from the Office for Budget Responsibility (OBR), which will be published after her Commons speech. The OBR, the independent body responsible for monitoring fiscal rules, traditionally assesses the governmentâ€™s fiscal plans twice yearly, but under new rules announced in Novemberâ€™s Budget, this assessment will now occur only once annually, at the autumn Budget. This yearâ€™s Spring Statement will therefore not include a formal fiscal rule assessment, marking a shift from past practice. The OBRâ€™s forecast will be released via the Treasuryâ€™s gov.uk platform following Reevesâ€™ speech, which is expected to begin shortly after midday. The government has implemented tighter controls after last yearâ€™s premature release of the OBR report, which led to the resignation of chairman Richard Hughes. The opposition is expected to respond, likely through Conservative leader Kemi Badenoch or shadow chancellor Mel Stride. Reeves is not anticipated to announce major tax or spending changes, as such decisions are reserved for the autumn Budget to avoid ongoing economic uncertainty. However, minor adjustments may be confirmed, as seen in last yearâ€™s statement, which included benefit changes later reversed. The Labour government, which took office in July 2024, prioritizes boosting economic growth. Recent data shows GDP grew 0.1% in the final quarter of 2025â€”slightly below expectationsâ€”and 1.3% for the full year. Inflation, while down from its 11.1% peak in October 2022, remains above target at 3% year-on-year to January, the lowest since March 2025, prompting expectations of a Bank of England interest rate cut from 3.75% in the coming month. Unemployment rose to 5.2% in the three months to December, the highest in nearly five years, while wage growth, excluding bonuses, stood at 4.2% annually. Reeves stated in February that 2026 would be the year the public begins to feel the benefits of Labourâ€™s economic reforms, asserting that growth conditions have been created and results are expected. Business leaders continue to express concern over the rising tax burden, particularly following the April 2024 increase in employer National Insurance contributions, which has raised hiring costs.

    [Original] Are you cut out for living and working in Antarctica?
    Dan McKenzie, 38, is the station leader at Halley VI Research Station in Antarctica, one of five facilities operated by the UKâ€™s British Antarctic Survey (BAS). A former marine engineer from Wigan, McKenzie transitioned from seafaring to polar work, drawn by the challenge of remote, extreme environments. His role oversees a team of 40 during the Antarctic summer season (November to mid-February), managing operations, health and safety, supplies, and emotional wellbeing. The station focuses on atmospheric and space research, ice shelf monitoring, and ozone layer studies. Temperatures range from -15Â°C in summer to as low as -40Â°C, with continuous daylight ending in a prolonged sunset. McKenzie, who began his Antarctic career in 2019 as a mechanical engineer at Rothera Station, emphasizes the importance of interpersonal support in close quarters, noting that isolation and shared living spaces can be more challenging than the cold. BAS employs around 120 people in Antarctica during summer, with up to 50 overwintering. Most staff return to the UK by May, though McKenzie has previously overwintered, describing the winter months as a unique sense of freedom within a tight-knit community. BAS recruits up to 150 new staff annually, with 70% in operational roles such as electricians, chefs, plumbers, medics, and hairdressers. Salaries start at Â£31,244, with travel, accommodation, meals, and extreme-weather gear provided. The selection process assesses conflict resolution and problem-solving, followed by rigorous training. While physical risks are significant, BAS HR head Mariella Giancola notes that lack of privacy and structured routines often challenge applicants, likening the experience to â€œgoing back to uni.â€ Clinical psychologist Dr Duncan Precious highlights that social dynamics can be more difficult than environmental hazards, though those drawn to Antarctica often thrive under â€œgood stress,â€ similar to military service. McKenzie acknowledges initial struggles with shared living and weather but now cherishes experiences like witnessing emperor penguin colonies and wildlife excursions. â€œThis is pretty brilliant,â€ he says, reflecting on the unparalleled natural beauty and contribution to environmental science.

    [Original] Unlicensed betting firms face sponsorship ban
    Image source, Getty ImagesImage caption, Bournemouth are one of several Premier League clubs sponsored by betting websites run by TGP Europe Gambling firms not licensed in the UK could be banned from sponsoring sports teams - including Premier League clubs - as part of a government crackdown. Ministers say they are worried about the risks stemming from the unlicensed market, such as companies not following laws and guidelines aimed at protecting customers. These include mandatory financial vulnerability checks and responsible advertising. The government also warns a lack of data protection measures can leave people open to fraud and identity theft and that unlicensed betting has been linked to organised crime. A consultation into the prosposals will be launched this spring. Last year, several clubs were warned by the Gambling Commission over their relationship with unlicensed TGP Europe. Premier League Bournemouth, Fulham, Newcastle and Wolves, as well as then-Championship Burnley, were all sponsored by betting websites run by the firm, which had surrendered its British licence after an investigation found it failed to "carry out sufficient checks on business partners" and breached "anti-money laundering rules". A letter sent to the clubs warned they "may be liable to prosecution... if they promote unlicensed gambling businesses that transact with consumers in Great Britain". Announcing the forthcoming consultation, Culture Secretary Lisa Nandy said people placing bets "deserve to know the sites they're using are properly regulated, with the right protections in place". She added: "It's not right that unlicensed gambling operators can sponsor some of our biggest football clubs, raising their profile and potentially drawing fans towards sites that don't meet our regulatory standards." In a post on social media site X, the Betting and Gaming Council backed the government's plan, writing: "It's not right that gambling companies without a UK licence can sponsor Premier League clubs. "If an operator wants the visibility and credibility of English football, they should meet the high regulatory standards set here in the UK." Premier League to limit gambling sponsors on shirts Published13 April 2023From beer to betting - how have football shirt sponsors changed? Published18 April 2025Four Premier League clubs warned over gambling sponsors Published16 May 2025Premier League clubs have previously collectively agreed to withdraw gambling sponsorship from the front of their matchday shirts by the end of this season. However, sleeve sponsorship can still carry gambling branding, including that of unlicensed firms, and the government warns that can give non-regulated companies "a major presence in the country's most-watched sports league". Ministers argue there is a "strong case for stopping unlicensed sponsorship altogether given the brand visibility could drive consumers towards unlicensed sites operating outside the Gambling Commission's regulatory protections". The commission estimates up to 1.4 million adults in the UK have a gambling problem, external. TGP Europe has been approached for comment. Get news, insight and fan views on your Premier League team

    [Original] Porn company fined Â£1.35m by Ofcom over age check failings
    ShareSaveLaura CressTechnology reporterShareSaveGetty ImagesOfcom has fined a porn company Â£1.35m for failing to introduce proper age verification measures on its websites. The media regulator said 8579 LLC's sites did not have "highly effective" methods to check UK visitors were over 18 and prevent children accessing the content. The fine - Ofcom's largest levied under the Online Safety Act (OSA) so far - comes after it began probing the firm "within days" of age check rules taking effect in July 2025. 8579 LLC has also been fined a further Â£50,000 for not responding to Ofcom's information requests. According to Ofcom, the company failed to implement highly effective age checks on most of its porn sites between 25 July and at least 19 November 2025. The regulator says 8579 LLC must implement robust methods to check UK visitors are over 18 on one remaining site before 17:00 GMT on Monday, or face an additional Â£1,000 daily penalty. George Lusty, director of enforcement at Ofcom, said it had "been clear" adult sites needed to deploy robust age checks to protect children in the UK form seeing porn. "Those that fail to do this â€“ or ignore legally binding requests from us â€“ should expect to face fines," he added. The regulator is also requiring 8579 LLC to provide Ofcom with a complete list of all sites it operates, after failing to respond to the regulator's information requests. It risks a further additional daily fine of Â£250 if it does not comply. Ofcom has already launched probes into many porn sites lacking age checks and handed down decisions, including fines, for some. In December it fined porn company AVS Group Ltd Â£1m for continued non-compliance with the OSA. Ofcom later said AVS had rolled out age checks on some of its porn sites. Meanwhile on 2 February, Pornhub began restricting access to its website in the UK. Aylo, Pornhub's parent company, said the OSA had "not achieved its goal of protecting minors". It also said the law had "diverted traffic to darker, unregulated corners of the internet". The Act is a set of laws and duties online platforms must follow, that are implemented and enforced by Ofcom. Under its Children's Codes, platforms must also prevent young people from encountering harmful content relating to suicide, self-harm, eating disorders and pornography.     [Original] Pentagon Summons Anthropic Chief in Dispute Over A.I. Limits
    Amid escalating pressure from the Trump administration, Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth has scheduled a meeting with Dario Amodei, CEO of artificial intelligence firm Anthropic, at the Pentagon to discuss the companyâ€™s use of its technology on classified military systems. The meeting follows a January 9 memo from Hegseth urging AI firms to remove restrictions on their models, prompting renegotiation of a $200 million pilot contract between the Pentagon and Anthropic. While the Defense Department has already signed an agreement with Elon Muskâ€™s xAI and is nearing a deal with Googleâ€”whose Gemini model is seen as a rival to Anthropicâ€”officials aim to use these agreements to pressure Anthropic into broader access. The Pentagon insists contracts must allow unrestricted use of AI models, as long as activities remain lawful, while permitting companies to retain safety features, known as â€œthe safety stack.â€ Anthropic, the first company authorized to operate on military classified networks, has expressed willingness to loosen restrictions but insists on guardrails preventing use in autonomous weapons without human oversight or mass surveillance of Americans. The company has also emphasized its efforts to block Chinese entities, including a November 2023 incident where it banned a Chinese-state-sponsored group using its technology in a cyber campaign targeting tech firms, financial institutions, chemical manufacturers, and government agencies. Earlier, OpenAI reported stopping two separate Chinese efforts to use AI for surveillance, and The New York Times has filed a lawsuit against OpenAI and Microsoft over the matter. Prior to Hegsethâ€™s meeting, Anthropic published a blog post revealing that three Chinese AI firms attempted to siphon data from its systems to enhance their own models. Pentagon officials acknowledge that removing Anthropic from classified systems would cause short-term disruptions, as military personnel regularly use its AI chatbot, Claude, alongside Palantirâ€™s data analytics tools for classified analysis. Experts argue cutting off access would be counterproductive. While xAIâ€™s model is considered less advanced than Anthropicâ€™s, Google is eager to secure a deal, having invested heavily in government-exclusive data centers that remain underutilized. OpenAI is not close to a classified contract, citing the need to further develop safety protocols. The meeting between Hegseth and Amodei was first reported by Axios. Cade Metz contributed reporting from San Francisco. Julian E. Barnes covers U.S. intelligence and international security, and Sheera Frenkel reports on technologyâ€™s impact on daily life, focusing on social media platforms.

    [Original] After Saks Bankruptcy, Richard Baker Says He Saved Luxury Department Stores
    Richard Baker, 60, is at the center of the collapse of Saks Global, the parent company of Saks Fifth Avenue, Neiman Marcus, and Bergdorf Goodman, which filed for bankruptcy in January 2025, just 13 months after its formation. Baker, who once described himself as an â€œentrepreneurâ€ focused on consolidating high-end retail through real estate value, claimed he extended the lifespans of struggling department stores by keeping them operational for a decade longer than expected, citing 50,000 employees working 500,000 additional work years. He blamed external pressuresâ€”economic strain, tariffs, and a Puck newsletter that allegedly caused vendors to withhold products due to payment fearsâ€”for the downfall. Saks Global has since shuttered 57 Saks Off 5th locations and all five Neimanâ€™s Last Call stores, with hundreds of jobs lost and brands like Chanel, Zegna, and Akris owed over $700 million. Bakerâ€™s track record includes acquiring Lord & Taylor in 2006 for $1.2 billion using $1.18 billion in debt, running it for 13 years before selling its flagship to WeWork in 2017 for $850 million. He later sold the retail arm to Le Tote in 2019 for $100 million, a company that filed for bankruptcy in 2020. In 2013, he bought Saks Fifth Avenue for $2.9 billion, securing a $1.25 billion mortgage on its Fifth Avenue flagship, valued at $3.7 billion. In 2023, he pursued Neiman Marcus, raising $2.2 billion in debt and $475 million in equity from Amazon, Salesforce, and Authentic Brands, promising $600 million in savings over five years. However, the combined company struggled with debt servicing, leading to delayed payments. In February 2025, CEO Marc Metrick informed brands that payments could be delayed by up to three months. Puck, an online newsletter, published critical reports on vendor payment issues, prompting Saks to file a lawsuit alleging â€œfalse and sensationalist reporting,â€ which remains ongoing. Critics, including former EstÃ©e Lauder executive John Demsey, called Bakerâ€™s ambitions â€œbravadoâ€ built on â€œflimsy ground.â€ While Baker maintains his vision was sound, many in retail see him as a symbol of the luxury department storeâ€™s decline, with investors, landlords, and brands bearing the cost.

    [Original] More Than Half a Million Customers Have Lost Power on East Coast
    Widespread power outages affected hundreds of thousands of customers across the East Coast as blizzard conditions brought high winds, heavy wet snow, and falling trees, damaging local power lines and poles. Approximately 650,000 electricity customers lost power, with Massachusetts experiencing the highest numberâ€”nearly 300,000â€”by early afternoon, according to Poweroutage.us. Coastal areas, particularly Cape Cod and southeastern Massachusetts, were hardest hit, with 66% of customers in Barnstable and 80% in Plymouth without power by noon. Wind gusts exceeded 60 mph, exacerbating damage and creating treacherous travel conditions. Despite the localized disruptions, regional grid operators reported normal conditions. ISO New England, which oversees the grid in Massachusetts, Connecticut, Maine, New Hampshire, Rhode Island, and Vermont, confirmed the transmission system remained stable. Similarly, PJM Interconnection, which manages the grid in New Jersey and parts of the Mid-Atlantic, reported no systemic failures. â€œThe regional grid remains in normal operating conditions and we have plenty of supply,â€ said Matt Kakley, a spokesperson for ISO New England. Outages were attributed to distribution-level issues, not grid-wide failures like those seen during Texasâ€™s 2011 winter storm. New Jersey also saw growing outages, with over 125,000 customers affected, as wind worsened weather conditions. Forecasters warned that accumulating wet snow and strong winds could cause further damage to power infrastructure. Eversource, a major utility serving Massachusetts and neighboring states, cautioned customers that restoration could take three to five days due to difficult travel conditions that hindered repair crews. The company sent automated alerts warning of prolonged outages. Residents without generators, home batteries, or backup heating faced heightened risks, especially with overnight temperatures expected to drop into the teens. In response, the town of Plymouth announced it would open an emergency shelter at a high school for those without heat. The stormâ€™s intensity and prolonged duration raised concerns about vulnerable populations and the resilience of local distribution systems. The situation underscored the difference between widespread grid failures and localized outages, with transmission infrastructure holding firm despite severe weather.

    [Original] Binance Employees Find $1.7 Billion in Crypto Was Sent to Iranian Entities
    Internal investigators at Binance uncovered that over 1,500 accounts had been accessed by individuals in Iran within the past year, with approximately $1.7 billion flowing from Binance accounts to Iranian entities linked to terrorist groups, including the Houthis and Iranâ€™s Islamic Revolutionary Guards Corps (IRGC), a U.S.-designated terrorist organization. The investigation, conducted in 2023, identified a Hong Kong-based firm, Blessed Trust, as a Binance fiat partner that facilitated $1.2 billion in crypto transfers to Iran-linked wallets over two years. Blessed Trust, incorporated in the British Virgin Islands and Cayman Islands, denied knowingly violating sanctions, stating its work with Binance involved only routine payments like payroll and invoice settlements. Binance confirmed it severed ties with Blessed Trust in January and reported the findings to U.S. authorities, including the Justice Department, in October. A separate investigation revealed that a defunct Hong Kong firm, Hexa Whale Trading Limited, funneled $490 million to Iranian-linked wallets, with Israeli officials alerting Binance to terror financing links. Binance also detected attempts to access accounts from sanctioned jurisdictions and identified Russian cargo ships using Binance accounts to pay crews, though the vessels were not sanctioned. Despite these findings, Binance fired or suspended at least four internal investigators in November and December, citing â€œviolations of company protocolâ€ related to unauthorized disclosure of client data. The company denied the suspensions were retaliation for raising compliance concerns, stating the actions were tied to data handling issues. Binanceâ€™s chief compliance officer, Noah Perlman, has reportedly considered leaving, and over half a dozen compliance staff have exited in recent months. The company maintains it has fulfilled its legal obligations, noting that detection of logins from sanctioned regions does not equate to servicing sanctioned persons. Binance, which pleaded guilty in 2023 to violating U.S. sanctions and paid a $4.3 billion penalty, has since hired over 60 former law enforcement and regulatory experts. The revelations come amid heightened scrutiny, including President Trumpâ€™s pardon of Binance founder Changpeng Zhao in 2024 and Zhaoâ€™s recent appearance at a Mar-a-Lago conference. White House press secretary Karoline Leavitt claimed Zhaoâ€™s prosecution was part of a â€œwar on cryptocurrencyâ€ by the Biden administration. Binanceâ€™s representative Rachel Conlan stated the company acted appropriately, emphasizing that the investigation continued after the suspensions and that no evidence of sanctions violations was found.

    [Original] More than 5,000 flights cancelled as US east coast digs out of record snow
    A major winter storm slammed the U.S. East Coast on Monday, bringing record-breaking snowfall, widespread power outages, and massive travel disruptions.     [Original] Rob Jetten becomes Netherlands' youngest ever PM
    Rob Jetten, 38, has become the youngest and first openly gay prime minister of the Netherlands, officially sworn in by King Willem-Alexander at Huis ten Bosch Palace in The Hague. His minority government, formed with the Peopleâ€™s Party for Freedom and Democracy (VVD) and the Christian Democratic Alliance (CDA), marks a significant political shift after a tightly contested October election in which D66 narrowly defeated anti-Islam populist Geert Wilders. Jetten succeeds Dick Schoof, whose government lasted just months, making it one of the shortest in Dutch history. The coalition, comprising seven D66 ministers, six from VVD, and five from CDA, with three state secretaries each, will govern as a minority cabinet, requiring vote-by-vote negotiation in both parliamentary houses for every major reform. Key policies include a â‚¬19bn (Â£16.6bn) increase in defence spending, cuts to healthcare and benefits, and a controversial plan to require asylum seekers to apply outside Europe rather than upon arrivalâ€”reflecting the sensitive nature of migration in Dutch politics, which contributed to the collapse of two previous governments. Jetten, once dubbed â€œRobot Jettenâ€ for his stiff TV appearances, has undergone a notable transformation, appearing relaxed and charismatic during election night celebrations in Leiden. His upbeat, pro-EU, and socially liberal stance contrasted sharply with Wildersâ€™ hard-right platform. While his sexuality was not a campaign issue in the Netherlandsâ€”indicating the countryâ€™s progressive stance on LGBTQ rightsâ€”globally, his appointment is a landmark moment for LGBTQ representation in leadership, offering inspiration in nations where coming out remains dangerous. Wilders, who dissolved his own coalition in June, has vowed to oppose all initiatives from Jettenâ€™s administration.

    [Original] Briton among 19 killed in Nepal bus crash
    ShareSavePhanindra Dahal,BBC Nepali, in Kathmandu,andHafsa KhalilShareSaveEPAA 24-year-old British man is among 19 people who were killed in a bus crash in Nepal, police say. The bus - which had been carrying tourists - had been travelling to the capital, Kathmandu, when it lost control and fell 200m on to the bank of the Trishuli river, in the country's central Dhading district, in the early hours of Monday morning. There were 44 people onboard including the driver, 25 of whom suffered injuries. The bus had been travelling from Pokhara, a popular tourist spot. Nepal's Home Ministry has created a five-member taskforce to investigate the cause of the incident. The UK Foreign Office said it was assisting the family of the Briton who was killed. Nepalese authorities identified him as Stewart Dominic Ethan. His name has not been confirmed by the Foreign Office. Nepalese police say they have identified all 19 bodies, including a 40-year-old Chinese woman and a 32-year-old man from India. Among the injured is a Chinese national and a New Zealander. All the injured had been taken to hospitals in the capital, they added. Children were among those onboard. Multiple teams were sent to the site, including police units, the army and a rescue team of divers, authorities said. Police spokesman Abinarayan Kafle said 17 people died at the scene, with two more dying while receiving treatment, BBC Nepali reported. Road accidents are relatively commonplace in Nepal, due to a range of factors including poor road maintenance and narrow paths in mountainous areas. In 2024, at least 14 people died after a bus travelling from Pokhara to Kathmandu fell into the Marsyangdi river in the Tanahun district. "We are supporting the family of a British man who has died in Nepal and are in contact with the local authorities," a Foreign Office spokesman told the BBC. Nepal is a popular destination for many international visitors, especially climbers, who travel there to access a key section of the Himalaya mountain range that includes Mount Everest. Home to eight of the world's tallest peaks, mountaineering is a significant source of revenue for the country - in 2024, climbing fees brought in $5.9m (Â£4.4m).

    [Original] Slovakia halts emergency power supplies to Ukraine over Russian oil dispute
    Slovak Prime Minister Robert Fico announced on February 23, 2026, that Slovakia will suspend emergency electricity supplies to Ukraine unless Kyiv resumes the transit of Russian crude oil through the Soviet-era Druzhba pipeline, which crosses Ukrainian territory. Fico made the announcement via a Facebook video, stating that â€œas of today, if the Ukrainian side turns to Slovakia with a request for assistance in stabilising the Ukrainian energy grid, such assistance will not be provided.â€ The move follows a social media ultimatum issued two days earlier, warning that state-owned SEPS would halt emergency power deliveries if oil flows did not resume. Ukraineâ€™s grid operator, Ukrenergo, confirmed it had not received formal notification but stated the suspension would not impact the unified power system. The last emergency request from Ukraine was over a month ago and involved limited volume. Fico said the electricity cutoff would be lifted â€œas soon as the transit of oil to Slovakia is restored,â€ warning of â€œfurther reciprocal stepsâ€ if not. He accused Ukraine of making a â€œpurely political decision aimed at blackmailing Slovakia over its international positions on the war in Ukraine.â€ The Druzhba pipeline was shut down in late January after Ukraine reported a Russian drone strike damaged infrastructure. Ukraine maintains it is repairing the pipeline as quickly as possible. Slovakia and Hungary, both still dependent on Russian oil since the 2022 invasion, blame Kyiv for the prolonged outage and have declared energy emergencies. The EU exempted the Druzhba pipeline from its 2022 ban on Russian oil imports to allow Central European nations time to transition. Meanwhile, the EU failed to agree on new sanctions against Russia for the fourth anniversary of the war, with Hungary vetoing the move. Hungarian Prime Minister Viktor Orban, a close ally of Moscow, is blocking a 90-billion-euro EU loan to Ukraine until the pipeline is reopened. Fico also refused to involve Slovakia in the upcoming EU loan, citing Zelenskyyâ€™s â€œunacceptable behaviour,â€ referencing Ukraineâ€™s decision to halt Russian gas transit after a five-year agreement expired on January 1, 2025. Fico claims this has cost Slovakia 500 million euros ($590 million) annually. According to Kyiv-based consultancy ExPro, Slovakia and Hungary have supplied 68% of Ukraineâ€™s imported power this month, though it remains unclear if emergency electricity was included in that figure.

    [Original] BBC criticised for nixing â€˜Free Palestineâ€™ tribute from BAFTA coverage
    British-Nigerian filmmaker Akinola Davies Jr, who won the BAFTA for outstanding debut by a British writer, director or producer for his film *My Fatherâ€™s Shadow*, sparked controversy after his acceptance speech was edited by the BBC.     [Original] Wassenaar Arrangement: will China join or kill this 30-year-old weapon control club?
    International regime controls defence tech exports but a push for self-reliance has seen Chinese weaponry surpass that of Western nations The Wassenaar Arrangement has long been seen as a symbol of Chinaâ€™s isolation from the global community.This major international regime controls the export of weapons and advanced technologies, and its 42 member states include nearly all developed Western countries, nations closely tied to China like Russia, and developing countries such as India. This year marks the 30th anniversary of the Wassenaar Arrangement. Ironically, Chinaâ€™s military technology has now caught up with â€“ and in some areas even surpassed â€“ that of Western nations.     [Original] Chinaâ€™s zero-tariff offer to Africa is a game changer
    In contrast to Western proposals that come with strings attached, China has turned its own market into the main instrument of partnership African nations have long been asking: who really opens their market, on what terms and how fast?     [Original] æ˜¥èŠ‚è¿”ç¨‹é«˜é€Ÿä¸Šæ¼”â€œå†°ç«ä¸¤é‡å¤©â€
    During the peak period of the Spring Festival return journey, national expressways across China exhibited a stark contrast of conditions. From February 15 to 17, strong snowfall and low temperatures affected North China, Northwest China, and Southwest China, leading to temporary traffic control on multiple expressways in Shanxi, Shaanxi, and Gansu provinces. Some sections experienced vehicle congestion, prompting emergency deployment of rescue forces. Meanwhile, major highways in the Yangtze River Delta, Pearl River Delta, and Beijing-Tianjin-Hebei region faced peak return traffic, with traffic volume on routes such as the Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Kunming, and Guangzhou-Shenzhen expressways exceeding 150% of their daily capacity. Some toll stations saw queues exceeding 5 kilometers, while service areas encountered difficulties with fueling and restroom access. According to monitoring by the Ministry of Transport, the combination of extreme weather and large-scale population movement highlighted structural contradictions in regional transportation infrastructure regarding emergency response and peak passenger handling. The northern regions' road closures due to ice and snow revealed shortcomings in snow removal equipment and emergency response capabilities, while southern congestion underscored inadequate holiday traffic management and public travel guidance. With the diminishing impact of the "celebrate the Lunar New Year locally" policy, return travel demand this year has significantly increased, intensifying traffic pressure. The transportation authorities have activated emergency mechanisms, dispatching additional clearance and snow removal teams, enhancing information dissemination and navigation guidance, and coordinating with service areas to increase supply of essential goods. Experts recommend accelerating the construction of intelligent transportation systems to improve dynamic network control, promoting staggered travel to alleviate traffic pressure during major holidays. The public is advised to closely monitor weather and road conditions before traveling, plan routes accordingly, and ensure a safe and efficient return journey.

    [Original] å¾·å›½æ€»ç†é»˜èŒ¨å°†è®¿å
    German Chancellor Friedrich Merz will soon undertake his first Asian visit since taking office, marking a further strengthening of Germany's foreign policy toward China. The visit comes at a time when Sino-German bilateral relations are undergoing adjustment and volatility, particularly against the backdrop of Europe's increasingly cautious approach to China, and is seen as a crucial opportunity to promote dialogue and restore economic and trade cooperation. In 2023, bilateral trade between China and Germany reached 200 billion euros, with China remaining Germany's largest trading partner for several consecutive years. However, due to geopolitical tensions, supply chain restructuring, and a stricter EU policy toward China, some German companies have adopted a more cautious stance on investing in China, and cooperation in key sectors such as new energy, semiconductors, and artificial intelligence has encountered obstacles. Merz's visit will focus on deepening economic and trade cooperation, advancing green transition and sustainable development, enhancing technological exchanges, and addressing global challenges such as climate change and energy security. According to German sources, the two sides may sign multiple cooperation agreements during the visit, covering areas including the electric vehicle supply chain, renewable energy technology collaboration, and digital infrastructure development. Merz will also hold strategic dialogues with senior Chinese officials to discuss building a stable and predictable bilateral relationship based on mutual respect. Analysts note that this visit could help ease tensions between China and Germany and provide a pragmatic reference for Europe's overall policy toward China. Against the backdrop of profound changes in the global landscape, Germany is sending a clear signal: Europe should not view China as a purely "adversary," but rather seek a balanced approach that combines competition with cooperation. If the visit yields substantial results, it could inject new stability into Sino-European relations.

    [Original] è¿”ç¨‹å®¢æµæŒç»­èµ°é«˜ å„åœ°å¼€å¯æŠ¤èˆªæ¨¡å¼
    On October 6, the national railway, road, civil aviation, and waterway systems transported over 280 million passengers, a nearly 15% increase from the previous day, setting a new record for daily passenger volume during this year's National Day holiday. Among them, the railway system transported approximately 85 million passengers, with major hubs such as Beijing West Station, Shanghai Hongqiao Station, and Guangzhou South Station each handling over 300,000 passengers daily on average. Popular routes including Beijing-Shanghai, Guangzhou-Shenzhen, and Chengdu-Chongqing remained in high demand, with tickets hard to obtain; some train services were temporarily added to cope with passenger pressure. To ensure smooth travel during the return peak, transportation departments across regions activated "escort mode": railway authorities increased night and weekend temporary trains, optimized passenger flow routes, and added directional signs and manned service counters; highway management units enhanced real-time monitoring, used variable message signs to issue congestion warnings, and coordinated with traffic police for trafficç–å¯¼; in civil aviation, major airports pre-deployed emergency response plans, increased check-in counters and security checkpoints, and some airports opened "fast-track inspection" channels. Many regions introduced combined solutions of "shuttle services + shared mobility," encouraging green travel options such as subways, buses, and ride-hailing services to alleviate pressure on urban main roads. Experts pointed out that this peak highlighted infrastructure shortcomings, including insufficient public transportation coverage in suburban and remote areas, and recommended accelerating the construction of intelligent transportation systems, enhancing emergency response capabilities, and establishing inter-departmental coordination mechanisms during holidays to achieve information sharing and resource integration. It is expected that October 8 will see the highest passenger volume, and relevant departments will continue to strengthen monitoring and service guarantees to ensure safe and orderly travel for the public.
